salutary/salutaire, bénéfique, utile/She always regarded even the very harshest honest criticism as a very salutary experience.
savings/économies, épargne/She had used all her very modest savings to purchase the most extraordinary and most rare old book.
prolong/prolonger, allonger, faire durer/She would never unnecessarily prolong any very important argument beyond what the evidence supported.
combining/combinant, associant, unissant/She was very brilliantly combining the very most different and most unexpected literary traditions.
caress/caresse, caresser/She brought a very wonderful caress of warmth and very great tenderness to every very difficult subject.
lovingly/amoureusement, tendrement, avec amour/She had very lovingly and very carefully preserved every single one of the most important old manuscripts.
ills/maux, problèmes, maladies/She wrote very powerfully about all the very greatest social and cultural ills of her remarkable era.
pier/jetée, pilier, pile de pont/She loved to walk to the very end of the old pier and think about her writing.
strayed/s'égara, a erré, dévié/She had very briefly strayed from her very main creative path but quickly found it again.
scarcity/rareté, pénurie/She wrote very movingly about the terrible creative scarcity that results from all forms of censorship.
wilful/délibéré, volontaire, entêté/She was wonderfully wilful in the very very best and most creative possible sense of the word.
emerging/émergent, qui surgit, qui se dégage/She was very rapidly emerging as the most important and most exciting new voice of her era.
redoubled/redoubla, a redoublé/She redoubled her very considerable efforts when the most important deadline suddenly moved much closer.
insisting/insistant, s'entêtant/She was very firmly and very clearly insisting on the absolute necessity of complete and total honesty.
rally/rassemblement, rallier, se reprendre/She made a very brave and very complete creative rally after the most difficult and discouraging period.
stroked/caressa, a tapé/She very lovingly stroked the beautiful old cover of the very precious and very rare old book.
cement/ciment, mortier, cimenter/She used the very most precise and most perfectly chosen language to cement her entire argument.
turmoil/agitation, tumulte, désordre/She remained very completely calm and very fully centred throughout the very greatest creative turmoil.
privacy/vie privée, intimité/She guarded her very extraordinary creative privacy with the most extraordinary care and determination.
perusal/lecture attentive, examen/She gave the very long manuscript a very careful and very thorough perusal before commenting.
reversed/renversa, a inversé, retourné/She very brilliantly reversed all the very most conventional expectations in the extraordinary new novel.
crave/désirer ardemment, avoir soif de/She always felt a very deep and very genuine creative craving for more knowledge and experience.
unsettled/perturbé, instable, agité/She felt very unsettled by the very unexpected and very surprising direction the work was taking.
jerk/secousse, saccade, secouer/She gave a very small jerk of recognition when she read the most extraordinary old passage.
pallor/pâleur, teint pâle/She noticed the very unmistakeable pallor of the most deeply exhausted and most overworked young writer.
stealthily/furtivement, subrepticement/She very stealthily and very carefully made her way through the very most complex argument.
meditating/méditant, réfléchissant/She sat very quietly meditating on the very most important and most significant aspects of the problem.
span/durée, envergure, enjamber/She covered an extraordinarily wide span of very different and very demanding creative territory.
wintry/hivernal, froid, glacial/She loved the very clean and very bracing quality of the most wintry and bleakest mornings.
twinkle/scintillement, étincelle, briller/She had a very warm twinkle in her very intelligent eyes when she told a very good story.
localities/localités, lieux, endroits/She had explored many very different and very extraordinary localities during her long creative life.
imprudent/imprudent, irréfléchi, téméraire/She was never imprudent in any creative decision however great the very exciting temptation.
sarcasm/sarcasme, ironie/She deployed the most brilliantly precise sarcasm against all very pompous and very pretentious criticism.
gayly/gaiement, joyeusement, allègrement/She gayly and very completely dismissed all very negative and very unproductive thoughts from her mind.
attitudes/attitudes, positions, postures/She described all the very different and very complex creative attitudes of her remarkable era.
exploring/explorant, en train d'explorer/She was always very eagerly exploring every very new and very unfamiliar creative territory.
leaps/bonds, sauts, fait des bonds/Her very extraordinary imagination always leaps to the most unexpected and most brilliantly vivid conclusion.
tackle/faire face, s'attaquer à, attirail/She would always very fearlessly tackle even the very most difficult and most demanding subjects.
chemistry/chimie, affinité/She described the very extraordinary creative chemistry between a very great writer and very devoted readers.
infamy/infamie, honte, ignominie/She wrote very powerfully about the very particular infamy of all deliberate creative dishonesty.
dictate/dicter, imposer, conditionner/She would never allow any very fashionable opinion to dictate the direction of her remarkable work.
flute/flûte/She had played the flute since her very earliest childhood and it informed all her very beautiful prose.
augmented/augmenta, a accru, renforcé/Her very considerable reputation was very greatly augmented by the extraordinary success of the new book.
exiled/exilé, banni, a exilé/She had been very creatively exiled by the most fashionable opinion but had triumphed completely.
pervaded/imprégna, a envahi/A very profound and very beautiful sense of quiet joy pervaded all her very finest writing.
scout/éclaireur, dénicher, reconnaître/She would very actively scout out every very new and very promising young literary talent.
criticisms/critiques, reproches/She listened very carefully to all the very most important and most helpful criticisms of her work.
experimental/expérimental, novateur/She had always embraced the very most experimental and the most daring of all creative approaches.
petals/pétales/She loved the very beautiful petals of the old roses that she kept on her writing desk.
uniforms/uniformes/She believed that very rigid literary uniforms were the enemies of all genuine creative thought.
confines/limites, frontières, restreint/She would never confine her very wide-ranging imagination within any very narrow or limiting boundaries.
heedless/insouciant, inattentif, inconscient/She was never heedless of the very great responsibilities that came with her remarkable creative gift.
remonstrance/remontrance, protestation/She listened very patiently to every very earnest and very heartfelt remonstrance before replying.
crumbling/s'effritant, qui s'effondre/She described the very slow crumbling of all the most very rigid and most limiting old conventions.
swarming/grouillant, fourmillant, essaimant/Her very fertile mind was very constantly swarming with the most extraordinary and exciting new ideas.
feasts/festins, fêtes, se régale/She feasts on every very new and very extraordinary book with extraordinary and very infectious enthusiasm.
cheque/chèque/She wrote the very generous cheque for the most important literary charity with very great pleasure.
contradictory/contradictoire, paradoxal/She found the very contradictory demands of public and private creative life very difficult to reconcile.
indifferently/indifféremment, de façon médiocre/She could never produce anything merely indifferently when the very extraordinary was clearly possible.
outlined/esquissé, a tracé, décrit à grands traits/She very carefully outlined the entire very complex structure before beginning to write a single word.
conveniently/commodément, opportunément/She had very conveniently arranged all her most important work into very clear and very ordered sections.
exaltation/exaltation, enthousiasme, transport/She felt a very deep and very genuine exaltation when the most difficult work was finally completed.
gowns/robes, tenues/She wore the very most simple and the very most elegant gowns to all very formal occasions.
tragedies/tragédies, drames/She had experienced many very great personal tragedies but had drawn on them all most powerfully.
vocabulary/vocabulaire, lexique/She had the most extraordinarily rich and the most brilliantly precise vocabulary of her whole generation.
swine/porcs, cochons, individus méprisables/She described the most aggressive and most contemptible critics as nothing but very literary swine.
shuddering/frissonnant, frémissant/She was shuddering with very cold and very genuine creative excitement as she wrote the final page.
unhappily/malheureusement, malheureux/She found herself very unhappily unable to finish the most important chapter before the deadline.
digits/chiffres, doigts/She counted on her very own digits all the many very extraordinary blessings of her creative life.
greed/avidité, cupidité, voracité/She described all the very greatest creative greed for new knowledge as a very wonderful quality.
tremor/tremblement, frémissement/She felt a very small but very distinct tremor of the most extraordinary creative excitement.
nave/nef/She loved to walk very slowly down the very long and very beautiful nave of the ancient cathedral.
clamour/clameur, vacarme, réclamer/She remained very completely serene above all the very considerable clamour of very hostile criticism.
infants/nourrissons, bébés/She wrote very beautifully about the very earliest and most tender experiences of all very young infants.
forenoon/avant-midi, matinée (archaïque)/She did all her very most important and very most difficult creative work during the forenoon.
onion/oignon/She grew the most wonderfully flavoured onions in her very productive and very carefully tended old garden.
pitiless/impitoyable, sans pitié, cruel/She was absolutely pitiless in her very careful elimination of every superfluous word from the text.
worrying/inquiétant, préoccupant, s'inquiétant/She found the very widespread decline in serious and careful reading genuinely and deeply worrying.
gayety/gaieté, enjouement, allégresse/She brought a very wonderful gayety and very great warmth to every single gathering she attended.
congratulations/félicitations/She received very warm and very genuine congratulations from all the most distinguished literary colleagues.
disabled/handicapé, désactivé, a rendu inutile/She wrote with very great compassion and very considerable insight about all disabled writers.
enchanting/enchanteur, charmant, ravissant/She had a truly enchanting way of bringing the very driest old subject completely to life.
thicker/plus épais, plus dense/The very old plot grew considerably thicker and very much more complex as the novel progressed.
warmest/le plus chaleureux, le plus chaud/She received the very warmest and the most genuinely moving welcome she had ever experienced.
examinations/examens, études, analyses/She had passed all her very most important academic examinations with the very highest possible distinction.
sages/sages, philosophes, sages personnes/She had read all the very greatest sages of every very different and very remarkable tradition.
amber/ambre, de couleur ambre/She loved the very beautiful amber light of the old lamp on her very old writing desk.
stiffly/rigidement, avec raideur/She moved very stiffly after the long creative effort but felt a very deep satisfaction.
oratory/éloquence, art oratoire, oratoire/She had a very remarkable gift for oratory that made her the most inspiring of public speakers.
everyday/quotidien, de tous les jours, banal/She found the very extraordinary hidden within every apparently very ordinary everyday experience.
rocking/berçant, oscillant, qui berce/She found the very gentle rocking of the old chair very deeply and very creatively soothing.
tarry/attarder, s'attarder, goudronneux (archaïque)/She would not tarry very long when there was so very much important creative work to be done.
grate/grille, râpe, grincer, irriter/She sat beside the old grate and watched the very warm and very cheerful fire burning.
inexperienced/inexpérimenté, novice, sans expérience/She was extraordinarily patient and very kind with even the very most inexperienced young writers.
impassioned/passionné, véhément, ardent/She gave the most extraordinarily impassioned and most completely convincing defence of literary freedom.
clapping/applaudissant, battant des mains/The entire very large audience was very enthusiastically clapping at the end of the brilliant reading.
gallows/gibet, potence, humour noir/She described the most extraordinary gallows humour of all the very finest literary black comedy.
practising/pratiquant, s'entraînant, exerçant/She had been very carefully practising and very greatly perfecting her craft for many long years.
oranges/oranges/She always kept a beautiful bowl of very fresh and very bright oranges on her writing desk.
sarcastic/sarcastique, mordant, ironique/She had a very brilliantly sarcastic wit that she deployed with extraordinary precision and great care.
fasting/jeûnant, jeûne/She described periods of creative drought as a very necessary and very purifying form of fasting.
polish/poli, lustre, polir, raffiner/She worked very hard to polish every single sentence until it gleamed with perfect clarity.
sensuous/sensuel, des sens/She had a very sensuous and very extraordinarily beautiful response to all the finest old language.
automatic/automatique, mécanique, instinctif/She would never allow her writing to become merely automatic or routinely mechanical.
hollows/creux, cavités, vallons/She described all the very beautiful and very mysterious hollows in the ancient and remarkable landscape.
geological/géologique, de géologie/She had a very fascinating and very detailed interest in all geological and natural history.
divides/divise, sépare, partage/She very clearly and very precisely divides the very most important from the very least significant.
unwelcome/importun, malvenu, indésirable/She received some very unwelcome but ultimately very salutary creative criticism from her trusted colleague.
priesthood/sacerdoce, clergé/She considered all the very greatest and most devoted writers to form a very sacred literary priesthood.
foretold/prédit, a prévu, annoncé/She had very clearly foretold the extraordinary direction that her very most remarkable generation would take.
kindest/le plus aimable, le plus généreux/She always found the very kindest and most encouraging way to make even the very hardest point.
overseer/surveillant, contremaître/She acted as the most extraordinarily careful and dedicated overseer of all her very best work.
capitals/capitales, majuscules, capitaux/She had visited many very great literary capitals during her very long and remarkable creative life.
resounded/résonna, a retenti/Her very extraordinary and most powerful voice resounded throughout the entire literary world of her era.
liberally/libéralement, généreusement/She always gave very liberally of her very considerable time to all who sought her advice.
quotes/citations, cite/She very carefully and very selectively quotes only the very most relevant and illuminating passages.
conclusive/concluant, décisif/She always provided the most conclusive and the most completely convincing evidence for every important claim.
chimneys/cheminées/She loved to watch the very beautiful old chimneys smoking in the early morning winter air.
murders/meurtres, tue, sabote/She writes about all the murders of literary truth with an extraordinary passion and very great anger.
effectively/efficacement, de façon effective/She very effectively and very brilliantly demolished the entire very elaborate critical argument.
unnoticed/inaperçu, non remarqué/She had remained very deliberately unnoticed for many years while producing her most extraordinary work.
wrap/envelopper, s'enrouler, emballage/She tried to wrap all her very most complex and difficult ideas in the clearest possible language.
anxieties/anxiétés, inquiétudes, soucis/She described all the very particular anxieties of the creative life with great honesty and humour.
consumer/consommateur, usager/She always thought of each very individual reader as something far more than a mere consumer.
blinding/aveuglant, éblouissant, qui aveugle/She received a very blinding and completely overwhelming flash of the most extraordinary creative inspiration.
curl/boucle, se recroqueviller, s'enrouler/She loved to curl up in her very favourite and most comfortable old chair with a book.
diseased/malade, malsain, gangrené/She described the most diseased and most corrupt aspects of literary culture with great directness.
classed/classé, catégorisé, rangé/She was always very classed among the very very greatest writers of her remarkable generation.
monkeys/singes/She described all the most imitative and least original critics as nothing but very literary monkeys.
naming/nommant, en nommant, appellation/She had a very extraordinary gift for very precisely naming even the most apparently nameless experience.
traitors/traîtres/She considered all those who betrayed literary truth to be the very worst of all creative traitors.
filial/filial, de fils ou de fille/She felt a very deep and very genuine filial affection for all the writers who had inspired her.
succour/secours, aide, secourir/She would always very generously offer succour and very warm support to any struggling writer.
thigh/cuisse/She found the most extraordinary old manuscript tucked into the very back of the very old thigh pocket.
destroys/détruit, anéantit/She destroys all the very most superfluous and the very most unnecessary words with great precision.
desertion/désertion, abandon, trahison/She described the very terrible sense of desertion felt by all very long-neglected literary genius.
entreaty/supplication, prière instante, imploration/She listened very patiently to every very sincere and very heartfelt entreaty before responding.
leafy/feuillé, boisé, vert/She loved the very beautiful and very cool shade of the leafy old avenue in summer.
walled/entouré de murs, cloisonné/She did her very best and most important creative work in the very quiet walled garden.

pricked/piqua, a piqué, pointu/She pricked up her very sensitive ears when she heard the extraordinary new and exciting idea.

invaluable/inestimable, précieux/She had received the most invaluable and the most completely transformative creative advice from her mentor.
threatens/menace, fait peser une menace/She very clearly threatens to leave the very fashionable literary world behind for good.
boisterous/turbulent, bruyant, agité/She remained very calm and completely composed throughout the most boisterous and heated critical debate.
receiver/receveur, récepteur, destinataire/She was considered the most devoted and most attentive receiver of all the finest old literary traditions.
revelations/révélations, découvertes/She had made several very extraordinary and very completely unexpected revelations in her most recent work.
ritual/rituel, rite, cérémoniel/She described the very beautiful and very necessary ritual of her daily and very disciplined writing.
beauteous/beau, magnifique (archaïque)/She described the very beauteous quality of the very finest and most perfectly crafted old prose.
curb/frein, bord du trottoir, maîtriser/She had learned to very carefully curb her very greatest and most excessive creative enthusiasms.
standpoint/point de vue, perspective/She always examined every very complex question from the very widest possible creative standpoint.
bends/courbes, virages, se penche, se courbe/She bends all the very most conventional rules of literary form to her extraordinary creative will.
horrified/horrifié, a horrifié/She was very deeply horrified by all the very deliberate and very callous destruction of books.
deputation/délégation, députation/She received a very formal and very distinguished deputation from the most important literary body.
openings/ouvertures, débuts, perspectives/She was extraordinarily gifted in the very difficult art of writing the most powerful creative openings.
ardently/ardemment, passionnément/She ardently and very passionately believed in the absolute necessity of all creative freedom.
conjectures/conjectures, suppositions/She never relied on mere conjectures but always based every argument on very solid evidence.
imports/importations, importe/She very carefully examines whatever she imports from other literary traditions to ensure quality.
rabble/populace, canaille, racaille/She described all the very noisiest and very least thoughtful critics as a mere literary rabble.
beak/bec, magistrat/She described her very precise and very perfectly chosen words as the very sharpest of all beaks.
degrading/dégradant, avilissant, déclassant/She found the very cynical exploitation of any creative talent to be completely and utterly degrading.
imaginable/imaginable, concevable/She had encountered every imaginable kind of creative difficulty and had overcome them all magnificently.
weaken/affaiblir, s'affaiblir/She would never allow any very harsh criticism to weaken her very deep and justified confidence.
